    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_feeda670-6132-4b8a-92fc-77326ce14e9c'

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-grumpy-with-a-candy-heart">trope-grumpy-with-a-candy-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-rep">lgbtq-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=disability-rep">disability-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2005341571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14604160039205353739"><b>Me, having absolutely no concept of liking things in moderation:</b> I WOULD DIE A THOUSAND FIERY DEATHS FOR THIS BOOK.<br/><br/>I feel like I need to dress up for reviewing this book, to take it in gratitude for a night out in someplace fancy, to offer it drinks. I’m so full of an unnamed wanting that I can’t bear it—like whatever I will allow to crawl out of my heart and down my arm and out my fingers is <em>not enough</em> because I just [clenches fist] love this series SO MUCH.<br/><br/>I first read <em>Vicious</em> a couple years a</span>
  <span id="freeText14604160039205353739" style="display:none"><b>Me, having absolutely no concept of liking things in moderation:</b> I WOULD DIE A THOUSAND FIERY DEATHS FOR THIS BOOK.<br /><br />I feel like I need to dress up for reviewing this book, to take it in gratitude for a night out in someplace fancy, to offer it drinks. I’m so full of an unnamed wanting that I can’t bear it—like whatever I will allow to crawl out of my heart and down my arm and out my fingers is <em>not enough</em> because I just [clenches fist] love this series SO MUCH.<br /><br />I first read <em>Vicious</em> a couple years ago, and I completely inhaled it. I read it again last year and afterward, it stayed inside my heart, setting me alight  from within like a candle flame. I was beyond excited for this sequel and I think my situation now is rather an object lesson in being careful what you wished for because that ending still presses hard into my ribs, making me feel simultaneously warm and sad. <strong>I NEED MORE.</strong><br /><br /><strong>
  <u>So what’s this book about?</u>
</strong><br /><br />Five years have made <strong>Victor Vale</strong>’s hatred of Eli Cardale lose its spark, its flame dampened by the fear introduced with Victor’s new unsettling reality: <strong>he keeps dying, again and again</strong>. Victor, it seems, has been torn and broken and put back together with half the pieces missing. He is desperate to not die, and even more than that, <em>to live</em>. In the collision of his whirling thoughts a plan begins to form, an architecture of gruesome messes that Victor will haul out in the hope of suturing himself back together. And Victor’s makeshift family—Sydney, Mitch, Dominic—is a lifeline to be tightly gripped…but things between them are falling apart in direct proportion to the rate at which Victor’s time is swirling away.<br /><br />Good luck doesn’t seem to be something that holds the hands of <strong>Eli Cardale</strong> these days either. Captured and imprisoned, he is left tormenting himself with the notion that his most desperate desires are just out of his reach, and one name leaps to mind above and before all others: <em>Victor</em>.<br /><br />Meanwhile, <strong>Marcella Riggins</strong>—a new EO—has made theater of murder in the town of Merit. Fear was her medium, and nightmares her art. She refuses to bow to fate and determines to embody the word that defines her: <strong>ruin</strong>. Marcella has upended the game board and sent the pieces flying, and many would wager that in all of time there had never been a purer wrath than hers. <strong>And she’s not alone</strong>; on her side is Jonathan, a taciturn human-shield, and June, a shapeshifter whose past is shrouded in secrecy and shadows.<br /><br />The one thing they all have in common? They’d all put themselves on top of a trapdoor going directly to the bowels of hell…with absolutely no way to unlatch it.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Power,” said the woman, “belongs to those who take it.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><strong>
  <em>VENGEFUL</em>
</strong> is a gripping and a staggeringly satisfying tightrope walk of a book. It’s so damn <em>good</em>. Though I’m not sure you’d call any of the people in it “good.” Within this ornately structured, reality-contorting framework, Schwab weaves together with a sure hand all the separate threads she's seeded along the way into a resoundingly orchestrated ending that will leave you wondering if healing is even remotely possible.<br /><br />Schwab wastes no time in bringing readers back into her massive, complex world—smartly beginning to expand her world outward into new dimensions, fleshing out new characters and seeing heads aflame, more than once.<br /><br />There are so many aspects of this book that leap out to me as brilliant: the introduction of women who were not beholden to the story of the men around them but rather had their own agency on full display, the examination of the grey spaces that exist between traditional definitions of good and evil, the terrifying and exhilarating situations, the whimsy and unsubtle darkness, the varied and wonderful character voices, Schwab’s love of antiheroes and her lilting voice, how she gives her characters power without the moral imperative to be <em>good </em>but does not allow them to slough off their culpability, how this book synthesizes the material in the previous book and gives it a new, different wholeness—<strong>all in one perfect book</strong>.<br /><br />There’s also something so captivating about the motley collection of punctured, unpredictable, darkly likeable individuals which makes up the heart of this book. Schwab is a skilled writer with a gift for voice and characterization. She makes every character a concrete individual with a definite presence. My old feelings for the recurring cast came softly thronging back, while I grew fond of new characters. I mean, look, they’re <em>all</em> terrible people, unmoored to any discernible first principles that guide their decision-making and always hoping for cruel ends to justify their brutal means but…¯\_(ツ)_/¯<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Maybe we are broken. But we put ourselves back together. We survived. That’s what makes us so powerful. And as for family—well, blood is always family, but family doesn’t always have to be blood.” </em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <u>VICTOR VALE:</u>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br /><br />I would take a bullet for my asexual fashionista foster father, Victor Vale. I know he’s all-too-powerful and doesn’t really need me to, but it just feels like the right thing to do.<br /><br /><strong>Victor Vale is one of the most interesting and complex characters I’ve ever come across.</strong> Schwab’s building of his character is as careful and subtle and clever as anything—though it’s sometimes easy to miss in the noise and gloss and intensity of his persona.<br /><br />Victor completely subverts both the hero and anti-hero archetype. He’s willing to do and has done anything to protect those immediately close to him and he is often surprised to find himself possessed by something perilously close to <em>affection</em> for them. But he’s not at all nice or soft—he’s cold and calculating and remorseless and gives an incredible illusion of sanity and stability but you never know what’s going on below his dispassionate mask. A lot of the things he’s done are irredeemable. Yet, you come to understand him deeply without being pushed to erase his past behavior. And while he does change in bursts and clashes (he’s shed enough of his selfishness to carve a place for Syd and Mitch, and he’s even less of a jerk to Dominic), <strong>he essentially doesn’t change at all</strong>.<br /><br />Our perception of him does, though. Victor’s desperation and the thrum of fear he’s constantly experiencing at the thought of irreversible death and leaving his family unprotected sort of humanizes him. I lived for those scattered smithereens of grudging vulnerability. Yet, somehow, I still feel like we’ll never know <em>all</em> the carefully cobbled pieces of him. There's just so much layers to his character and it's positively riveting!<br /><br />This is my way of reiterating: <strong>I NEED MORE</strong>.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <u>ELI CARDALE:</u>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br /><br />Well, he's alive and well…much to my chagrin.<br /><br />I haven’t quite parsed out my own relationship to Eli’s character but here’s the thing: part of me wants to believe that maybe, just maybe, the man who’s deception steeped in elegance, from his sharp smile to his unsettling eyes, malefic, hate-ravaged and bent on vengeance, is only a piece of who Eli is.<br /><br />Because over the course of this book, we are transported by the narrative back to Eli’s childhood and all that youthful hubris and quick-tempered rage and holier-than-thou drivel is swept away to reveal a deeply damaged individual whose life had come to him tangled in hate, and when he’d tried to untangle it, he’d failed. How he got there, and how the youth became this man, is one of this book’s most intriguing mysteries, pulling you ever deeper into the story. Another part of me, though, wishes I could root through my memories and shred my knowledge of his backstory—those years with his father’s vicious, careless cruelties and his mother’s indifferent neglect. Because Eli is<em> so horrible</em>. But I can't. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Once upon a time, when the marks on his back were still fresh, Eli told himself that he was growing wings. After all, his mother thought Eli was an angel, even if his father said he had the devil in him.” </em>
</blockquote><br /><br />Also, I feel like I’ll never stop feeling the scorch of acute nostalgia for when Eli and Victor had been better at loving each other, and worse at getting in one another’s way. And it’s frightening—in a really visceral way—the realization that everything could go wrong so horrendously, so quickly, and that, in the wrong circumstances, anyone might become a monster.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <u>MARCELLA MORGAN:</u>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br /><br />You know what? I want more Byronic women figures. I want more self-important, reckless women libertines in silk dresses and steel-heeled stilettos leaving a string of broken men in their wake while dashing off threats and coolly bargaining with rivals who wish to gnaw on their souls.<br /><br />I want more women characters with an utter, unflinching embrace of self who are just on the charming, mercurial side of unlikeable assholes—definitely unreliable and more often than not morally questionable.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Perhaps she was glass. But glass is only brittle until it breaks. Then it’s sharp.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />To say that Marcella is an intemperate, murderous lunatic would wound the feelings of most intemperate, murderous lunatics. And I am still a bit embarrassed about this next part—as it speaks to a black part of my character—but I would gladly let her step on my throat.<br /><br /><strong>Her character is so fascinating to me.</strong> Marcella is a study in brutality, a paragon of sheer and untampered force. She does not take things in, she only spins them around, sharpening them into weapons and recklessly flinging them right back. The men in her life couldn’t accept the idea that women are supposed to be multidimensional. They were happy to have her because they were happy with weakness. The more pliable a leader was, the more power they had. And who could be more pliable than a simple woman, playing at dominance?<br /><br />But Marcella wielded that ignorance like a finely knapped glass-knife. She pushed back against what the world decided for her. She was going to play the lead role in the grand cosmic drama, and not merely a bit part with no lines. She  required no validation. Her wish was her command. Her voice was her own; she uses it. Her life was her own; she carved a place for it. She was relentless in her dedication to herself. And she would never again allow weakness or softness, fear or ineptitude to hold her frozen. She hadn’t really known yet what she was capable of. And her gift had been untested.<br /><br />Until it wasn't.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“How many men would she have to turn to dust before one took her seriously?” </em>
</blockquote><br /><br />I also <em>have</em> to talk about Mitch and Syd.<strong> I love them</strong>. I would lay down both of my kidneys for Sydney. And we all know Mitch is so buff because all his muscles are filled with love. He's probably at the gym, furiously doing weights, and thinking “I’m going to be <em>so fucking good</em> at hugging.” WHAT AN ANGEL.<br /><br />I'm not gonna lie, the only thing sustaining me right now is the elaborate, self-indulgent fantasy version that I’ve created in my mind of a world where Victor, Syd, Mitch and their thrice-dead dog are safe and together and away from <b>*gestures vaguely*</b> <em>all this</em>.<br /><br /><blockquote>✨ <a href="http://amzn.eu/9Jnbkf3" rel="nofollow noopener">wishlist</a> ✨ <a href="https://runawaywithdreamthieves.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ✨ <a href="https://twitter.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ✨ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ✨</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="14604160039205353739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1420372287" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1420372287" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1420372287?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1420372287" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6042433586719031144"><blockquote><i>His eyes met Victor’s, and for a second neither man moved.</i><br/>Run, <i>thought Victor, and he could see the response in Eli’s coiled frame.</i><br/>Chase me.</blockquote><br/><b>Oh, how I loved this book</b>! I've waited five long years for the sequel to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40874032.Vicious__Villains___1_' title='Vicious (Villains, #1) by V.E. Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vicious</a> and I was starting to think it would never happen... but <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26856502.Vengeful__Villains___2_' title='Vengeful (Villains, #2) by V.E. Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vengeful</a> was so so good. Definitely worth the wait.<br/><br/>This duology (series??) is called "Villains" and yet the characters are so much more interesting than that. While I've enjoyed a number of Schwab's books, I feel like her </span>
  <span id="freeText6042433586719031144" style="display:none"><blockquote><i>His eyes met Victor’s, and for a second neither man moved.</i><br />Run, <i>thought Victor, and he could see the response in Eli’s coiled frame.</i><br />Chase me.</blockquote><br /><b>Oh, how I loved this book</b>! I've waited five long years for the sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40874032.Vicious__Villains___1_" title="Vicious (Villains, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a> and I was starting to think it would never happen... but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26856502.Vengeful__Villains___2_" title="Vengeful (Villains, #2) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vengeful</a> was so so good. Definitely worth the wait.<br /><br />This duology (series??) is called "Villains" and yet the characters are so much more interesting than that. While I've enjoyed a number of Schwab's books, I feel like her strongest writing and characters lie here with Victor and Eli. These "villains" are actually complex antiheroes - murderous and power-hungry, for sure, but also sympathetic and even likeable. They fascinate me.<br /><br />The bare bones of the story is not that original. I've read countless books about people with X-Men like powers. And yet, for me, Schwab makes this book stand out from the pile. She creates such interesting, well-rounded characters, and draws out the tension so perfectly that I <i>need</i> to know what happens next. I love it when an author can take an exhausted topic and breathe new life into it.<br /><br />In this book, new characters emerge to make the fight even bigger than before. Once again, we are forced to consider what it is to be good, to do right, and what it is to be evil. All of the characters do despicable things and yet their motives make a certain kind of sense-- even if I'm reluctant to admit it. The addition of a new character - Marcella - is a real highlight of this book. She is seriously terrible. And also freaking awesome.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Perhaps she was glass.<br /> But glass is only brittle until it breaks.<br /> Then it’s sharp.</i>
</blockquote><br />In fact, the female characters are far bigger stars in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26856502.Vengeful__Villains___2_" title="Vengeful (Villains, #2) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vengeful</a> than they are in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40874032.Vicious__Villains___1_" title="Vicious (Villains, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a>. <b>Hell hath no fury like women seeking vengeance against the men who wronged them.</b> June is another fantastic character and her snark made me smile with delight:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Whatever you’ve heard,” said June, “it’s probably true.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26856502.Vengeful__Villains___2_" title="Vengeful (Villains, #2) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vengeful</a>'s timeline jumps back and forth and all around, and frequently switches perspective. While less-skilled authors would probably give me whiplash with this, Schwab uses it really well. As the past races alongside the present, the tension increases until finally all the pieces come together. Never has the phrase “the past is catching up with you” been more appropriate.<br /><br />Between the new characters causing havoc and the inevitable confrontation between Eli and Victor, this book is just so addictively good. Eli's backstory made me love/hate him even more and Sydney's growth added another layer to the story. It was also great to have Victor confirm his asexuality on-page.<br /><br />It's such a good book, but I want to issue a quick warning so potential readers can make an informed decision: It's an adult book, with graphic violence and semi-graphic sex. Further <b>content warnings for:</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[domestic violence; attempted rape; drug use; suicide; graphic torture. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6042433586719031144" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria Schwab" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria Schwab" href="/user/show/1695365-victoria-schwab">Victoria Schwab</a>

If you follow me at all online, you know what this book took from me in terms of blood, sweat, tears, and sanity, and how proud I am of the finished product. I'd be honored to have your vote!</span>

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_1973352450'><a id="like_count_review_1973352450" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1973352450?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">3111 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F26856502-vengeful">Like</a></span>

<div id="review_1544741945" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1544741945" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1544741945?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781785652486" href="/book/show/40139338-vengeful">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=feminist-as-fuck">feminist-as-fuck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=finished-series">finished-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1544741945" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3411131328952270041"><i>“I don't want to survive. I want to thrive.”</i><br/><br/>Am I Victor Vale yet cause I can assure you that I died several times during the course of this book.<br/><br/>After wiping cold sweat off my forehead and 5 minutes of deep and thorough breathing exercises I am relieved and happy to tell you that I loved <i>Vengeful</i>. I had high hopes, but my fears were taller. Ever since Victoria had announced that she would write a sequel to <i>Vicious</i>, I wondered whether this was a good idea. Don't get me wrong, I loved the first bo</span>
  <span id="freeText3411131328952270041" style="display:none"><i>“I don't want to survive. I want to thrive.”</i><br /><br />Am I Victor Vale yet cause I can assure you that I died several times during the course of this book.<br /><br />After wiping cold sweat off my forehead and 5 minutes of deep and thorough breathing exercises I am relieved and happy to tell you that I loved <i>Vengeful</i>. I had high hopes, but my fears were taller. Ever since Victoria had announced that she would write a sequel to <i>Vicious</i>, I wondered whether this was a good idea. Don't get me wrong, I loved the first book, but that was the exact reason why I wanted it to keep being a standalone novel. It was perfect. I loved it from start to finish, I could not find a single thing that bothered me, I was in awe with every single aspect of this book. Victoria is one of my favourite authors and I knew that she could write. Her writing, her characters, her stories are exceptional. And still, I had my doubts. I was not the biggest fan of  and the finale to the <i>Shades of Magic</i> series was not as satisfying as I had wished.<br /><br />But then I opened the book and read the first page and I knew it, I knew this was the shit. This was going to be exactly what I wanted even though I had not known that I wanted it in the first place.<br /><br />Let's talk about the characters.<br />I don't like Eli. He was a reckless fanatic and I wanted him to die. I didn't care for Victor. He was equally violent but at least not as self-righteous as Eli. My heart was always with Sydney, Doll, and Mitch. I want them to stay safe forever.<br />Vengeful introduced me to Marcella, whom I loved from the very beginning. Her morals might have been even lower than those of Victor and Eli but I couldn't care less. June was another character I fell in love with. But she was not without issues either. However, I kind of like that her story was not explored in this book. We got hints, but her backstory is still draped in shadows...so if Victoria is actually going to write a third Villains book in five years - she said she might release a Villains book every five years - we might get to see more of June. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And Sydney. But luckily not Eli, I'm pretty sure of that and not sad about it. What I am sad about is that Marcella was killed off. I understand why - she was too powerful and would have raised hell so her influence had to be limited - but she was a fascinating character.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The way this story was constructed was a work of art. Victoria managed to assemble an impressive amount of POVs, each with their own voice. Things could have easily become unrealistic or rushed, but Victoria managed to maintain the pacing and the result was a thrilling, breathtaking story about villains, power and death. I know that it took a lot of patience and willpower to write this book but it was worth it. 5 well-deserved stars.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/kaispellmeier/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3411131328952270041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15735485087229487432">Okay. I'm gonna be a big brave girl and say it. <br/>This wasn't that great. <br/>There, I said it. <br/><a href='http://it.tinypic.com?ref=ok3ibl' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/><br/><br/>I mean<br/>-yes, I liked it. <br/>-yes, Victoria Schwab could write assembly instructions and I'd still read every word like it was prose. <br/>-yes, it was great to be back into the Villains universe. <br/>-yes, it was entertaining and made me lose my mind. <br/>-and yes, I still think Mitch should adopt us all. <br/><br/>But I can't say I loved Vengeful as much as I loved Vicious because it'd be </span>
  <span id="freeText15735485087229487432" style="display:none">Okay. I'm gonna be a big brave girl and say it. <br>This wasn't that great. <br>There, I said it. <br><a href="http://it.tinypic.com?ref=ok3ibl" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1538409040ra/26383676.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Phew. That was a hard one to admit. <br><br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/dXXz" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1586100549i/29236937._SX540_.jpg" alt="banner-di-bobi.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>I mean<br>-yes, I liked it. <br>-yes, Victoria Schwab could write assembly instructions and I'd still read every word like it was prose. <br>-yes, it was great to be back into the Villains universe. <br>-yes, it was entertaining and made me lose my mind. <br>-and yes, I still think Mitch should adopt us all. <br><br>But I can't say I loved Vengeful as much as I loved Vicious because it'd be a lie. <br>I don't know if I should believe the tingling and bothering feeling in my brain that suggests that maybe this one suffered from the sequel curse, or if the disappointment comes from it being too long &amp; packed with side characters/plots I couldn't get myself to fully care about, but I didn't feel the same enthusiasm I did last year, when Victor, Syd, Eli and their merry brigade came into my life.<br>I have no idea what happened. Somewhere between the first and the last chapters I got lost (and a bit bored sigh) and couldn't focus on it properly, despite the twists and raw scenes.<br>I felt like something was missing and, at the same time, something was imposing. <br>I guess I'll figure out what exactly didn't do it for me, someday. <br>But, man, what a pity. <br><s>And what a slip.</s><br><br>Don't get me wrong, Vengeful is still far from the tragedy that are many overhyped sequels out there, and I've still loved parts of it that I'll maybe gush about once the spoiler alert is at its minimum, but I still think Vicious was better. <br>And, if possible, sort of different. <br><br><br><br>@ Victoria Schwab, I still love you to pieces.<br>Please, don't ever stop writing.<br>Please, don't hate me.<br><a href="http://it.tinypic.com?ref=v80ciu" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_1955566596" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1955566596" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1955566596?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765387523" href="/book/show/37534835-vengeful">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2018">z-read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2018">y-out2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-squads">favorite-squads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2018">z-faves2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-pn-urban-fantasy">sff-pn-urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=plot-twists">plot-twists</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1955566596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4449454240991724933"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Men look at anyone with power and see only a threat, an obstacle in their path. They never have the sense to see power for what it really is. Potential.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>Vengeful</i> was my second most anticipated book of this year, and it did not disappoint at all. It was absolutely a wild ride and I read it in, literally, two sittings within the same day. S0 let’s scream!<br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>➽G O D, T H A T ’ S G O O D</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>I think Schwab’s writing style for <i>Vicious</i> is the best of every talent she has in the writing</span>
  <span id="freeText4449454240991724933" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Men look at anyone with power and see only a threat, an obstacle in their path. They never have the sense to see power for what it really is. Potential.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><i>Vengeful</i> was my second most anticipated book of this year, and it did not disappoint at all. It was absolutely a wild ride and I read it in, literally, two sittings within the same day. S0 let’s scream!<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>➽G O D, T H A T ’ S G O O D</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />I think Schwab’s writing style for <i>Vicious</i> is the best of every talent she has in the writing department; she’s abstract, a wide world without clear boundaries, but with enough detail that it’s hard not to be enthralled. <br />The ease with which I visualized scenes was just incredible; in this series especially, I think she does a really good job conveying the image of a scene without being too specific. <b>
  <i>SPOILER</i>
</b>: The Syd/Victor scene on the balcony, the tea shop scene with Syd &amp; June, and the scene in which a brick <i>almost</i> falls on Marcella all stuck out in my head in different ways.<br /><br /><blockquote><b><i>VENGEFUL's three female leads are a woman who can ruin anything--and anyone--she touches, a living voodoo doll, and a girl who can resurrect the dead. This book was made for 2018.</i></b>-<a href="https://twitter.com/veschwab/status/974026934668742662" rel="nofollow noopener">V.E. Schwab via Twitter</a></blockquote><br />The power of women in this book is just so, so real. Schwab plays around with terrifying yet strangely compelling female villains, and sympathetic female villains, and complex female leads, and it’s just all gorgeous. <br /><br />All that is fantastic, but besides my absolute love for the writing, why did I read this so quickly and become so enthralled? <b>The characters.</b> God I fucking love how she makes every character dynamic and interesting through just a few words, just a little hint of knowledge about them conveyed so beautifully and immediately you feel that you understand this character and that you root for this character. <br /><br />Okay, so, here’s a quick rundown of all the sides and characters: <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>➽V I C T O R, M I T C H, S Y D N E Y </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />→<b>
  <i>Victor Vale</i>
</b> - one of the best well-intentioned villain-from-one-point-of-view characters of all time. <br />→<b>
  <i>Sydney</i>
</b> - a slow-aging teenager who can bring back the dead. a legend and a queen and i love her. <br />→<b>
  <i>Mitch</i>
</b> - Victor’s sidekick, with no powers. the purest person in this book by all measures.<br />→<b>
  <i>Dol</i>
</b> - the ever-resurrecting dog. the only other pure being.<br />→<b>
  <i>Dom</i>
</b> - a far more unwilling sidekick who can step outside time and is Done With This Shit. I actually love Dom. <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>➽E L I E V E R</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />→<b>
  <i>Eli Ever</i>
</b> - is immortal and has also been through some shit, and he is <i>ready to kill</i>.<br /><br />Everyone said I would learn to sympathize with Eli this book, and you know what, you were all correct. I've always thought Eli made a fantastic villain, but his character writing here really hit a STRIDE.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>➽M A R C E L L A &amp; J U N E </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />→<b>
  <i>Marcella</i>
</b> - former wife of a gangster who can quite literally erode people.<br />→<b>
  <i>June</i>
</b> - a human voodoo doll. I have <i>no idea</i> what to make of her but I know I love her.<br />→<b>
  <i>Jonathan</i>
</b> - a strangely forgettable character but oh well - that’s the point. <br /><br />I loved the presence of such complexity in the villains here, and how well these three sides were integrated into the broader plot. The sheer character juggling here is really is impressive. <br /><br />Between <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1902165598" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a> and this, I really, really am in love with this series - it's my favorite by her without competition. <br /><br />✨ buddyread with most of goodreads, probably<br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/c/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4449454240991724933" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3317627661" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3317627661" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3317627661?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781785658631" href="/book/show/42635580-vengeful">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3317627661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11595145684621633325"><i>“Some people were matches, a bit of light and no heat. And some were furnaces, all heat but little light. And then, once in a blue moon, there was a bonfire, something so hot and bright you couldn't stand too near without burning.”</i><br/><br/>I loved this so much!! And I’m saying this not only because I’m Victor Vale trash - which I obviously am - but because V.E. Schwab knows how to tell a story! The way <b>“Vengeful”</b> was told is nothing but amazing. We have four weeks ago in the present, we have the past and</span>
  <span id="freeText11595145684621633325" style="display:none"><i>“Some people were matches, a bit of light and no heat. And some were furnaces, all heat but little light. And then, once in a blue moon, there was a bonfire, something so hot and bright you couldn't stand too near without burning.”</i><br /><br />I loved this so much!! And I’m saying this not only because I’m Victor Vale trash - which I obviously am - but because V.E. Schwab knows how to tell a story! The way <b>“Vengeful”</b> was told is nothing but amazing. We have four weeks ago in the present, we have the past and the longer the story proceeds the closer we get to the actual present events and the final climax of the story. And yes, I chose my words carefully here because while reading the book I couldn’t help but find parallels to Victor’s condition.<br /><br /><b>“Vengeful”</b> builds up like one of Victor’s energy charges and after the discharge you’re as drained and dizzy as him. This book however isn’t only about Victor but also about Eli, Sydney and Mitch. There are a lot of new players that enter the scene, like for instance Marcella, June and Jonathan. Not to mention all the countless EO’s EON found and arrested as well as the ones Victor found and ... well you know Vic doesn’t do things by halves. ;-P Neither does Eli, so it was only a matter of time until our old friend began scheming once again. <br /><br />This time it’s not all about Victor and Eli though and I was really happy to discover that we got a lot of female power to counterbalance our two boy’s ongoing feud! XD Believe me when I say that every single one of those characters has their own agenda and that they are not squeamish when it comes to enforcing their ambitions. We basically get a gathering of ruthless and powerful people who literally walk over dead bodies in order to achieve their goals and do I even need to say it? Yes? Well, my inner faerie had a field day! *lol* And before I go on and on, I better head to my character’s section and gush over there! ;-)<br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>You know what they say about Rome? All roads lead to Rome. Well, in this case it’s Merit so: Welcome to Merit! The city in which Victor Vale and Eli Ever started their vicious and vengeful vendetta. Tread carefully when you enter, you might get right smack into the middle of their fight and parts of spoilers could hit you at every corner! Consider yourself warned.</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Victor Vale:</b><br /><br /><i>”He had craved a lot of things – power, revenge, control – but sex was never one of them. Even with Angie... he’d wanted her, of course, wanted her attention, her devotion, even her love. He’d cared about her, would have found ways to please her – and perhaps found his own pleasure in that – but for him, it had never been about sex.”</i><br /><br />First things first: I still <u>LOVE</u> and <u>ADORE</u> Victor Vale. &lt;33 His character was every bit as intriguing and morally grey as it was in “Vicious” and it was such a pleasure to watch his mind at work. I was glad to discover that his habit of using text markers to blot out words hadn’t changed, even though I’ve to admit that – in this context – it broke my heart. Victor is all about logic and control and in “Vengeful” the two things he always relied on were taken away from him. He has no control over his body’s degeneration and even though he knows that he’s doomed the solution-oriented part of him just can’t accept his predicament. He’s a man on a mission and once he sets his mind to something he just can’t let it go. The truth is Victor clings to his life because he actually wants to live! He doesn’t want to leave Sydney or Mitch behind and he’s desperate to find a cure. It hurt to see him struggle and to know that he was just a shadow of his former self, but after that ending I have hope again! Maybe Victor will have a comeback in book three?! Please?! *asks nicely* <br /><br /><i>”You’re such a weirdo sometimes.”<br />“Only sometimes?” asked Victor. “I’ll have to try harder.” Those blue eyes flicked to Eli. “Normal is overrated.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Look at me,” he said coldly, catching Sydney’s chin in his hand. “The next time you point a gun at someone, make sure you’re ready to pull the trigger.”</i> <br /><br /><i>”Victor was used to being the strongest person in the room, and it was both familiar and unsettling to see that confidence on someone else.”</i><br /><br /><b>Sydney:</b><br /><br /><i>”Victor haunted her. His pain haunted her. His dying haunted her.<br />Because it was Sydney’s fault.”</i><br /><br />Ahh little Sydney has grown so much over those last five years! It was good to see that she became a part of Victor’s little family and that they got along so well. (Well is a loosely used term though because they are a super dysfunctional family but it somehow works? *lol*) If you ask me I don’t think that Sydney doesn’t age, I think that she does, but she does it very slowly. Maybe it has to do with the ice? It could have slowed down her metabolism and therefore she’d age really slowly? The concept of cryo-preservation exists for a reason after all. ;-) Also it was good that she worked on her abilities. I’m curious to find out what she might be able to do after she had some years to get accustomed to her powers. Hopefully I’ll be able to see it in the third book. XD Plus, I think now that she made peace with Serena’s death it might be easier to handle her powers. The emotional trauma of losing her sister might have influenced her abilities and I can’t wait to see her really grow into them. <br /><br /><b>Eli Ever:</b><br /><br /><i>”Eli’s faith had faltered in that room.<br />He had found Hell in that room.<br />And the only sign of God was that, no matter what Haverty did, Eli continued to survive. <br />Whether he wanted to or not.”</i><br /><br />I hate that I feel sorry for him, but since this was obviously Schwab’s intention I can blame it all on her. *lol* No, seriously. No one deserves to have a Dr. Haverty in their life and what he did with Eli was just cruel and inhuman. It was torture and no matter what Eli did it was wrong to experiment on him. Of course to some degree a person like Haverty was necessary to find Eli’s weaknesses and to explore them, because otherwise there would have been no way to stop him if he ever escaped. Which he ultimately did and Dr. Haverty was there to provide a solution. So yeah, I actually saw that one coming so I wasn’t surprised by the ending. Still, there were other things I didn’t expect: For instance Eli’s past. I began to wonder if he might have become a different person if his father wouldn’t have hurt him so much. How many of the things he believed were indoctrinated? How would he have turned out if his father’s religious fanaticism wouldn’t have shaped his thinking so much? It boggles the mind if you think about it too hard. In the end Eli was nothing but a little boy that got hurt by his own father and this actually made me really sad. =((<br /><br /><i>”He prayed that the pastor would stop seeing whatever he saw, while he carved new feathers into the torn wings of Eli’s back.”</i> <br /><br /><b>Marcella:</b><br /><br /><i>”How many men would she have to turn to dust before one took her seriously?”</i><br /><br />Now, if Marcella wasn’t the embodiment of a femme fatale, then I really don’t know! XD That woman was burning like a wildfire and consuming everything in her path. And just like a wildfire she wasn’t put out easily. ;-) Which quite honestly, only made me love her character even more. *lol* I liked the idea of a strong and independent female villain that strove for more than life was willing to offer her and I was glad she posed a real threat to Stell. Hell, Marcella even posed a threat to Eli and he was basically what you would call “extremely hard to kill”. Plus that woman had style! She took what she wanted and did it openly without hesitation. It’s rare to find a villain like that, especially a female one, which is just one more reason to love her for it! XD It’s a shame Eli managed to kill her, but without Jonathan she would have never been able to hold out for so long. <br /><br /><i>”She was done playing by other people’s rules. Done hiding. If you lived in the dark, you died in the dark. But stand in the light, and it was that much harder to make you disappear.”</i><br /><br /><i>”And what happens then?”<br />“Oh,” mused Marcella, tracing the veins in the stone, “I imagine that Director Stell will decide I’m more trouble than I’m worth.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Jesus, Marcella, anyone ever told you that you’re batshit crazy?”<br />Marcella pursed her lips. “Several times,” she said. “It’s an insult men love to aim at ambitious women.”</i><br /><br /><b>June:</b><br /><br /><i>”I saw became I think I saw became I couldn’t have seen became I didn’t see. Eyes were fickle. Minds were weak.”</i> <br /><br />Okay, let me say it: HOW COOL ARE JUDE’S POWERS???!!! OMG! A living shape shifting voodoo doll!!! Gosh, I’d love to have abilities like that!!! She can’t only change into every kind of person she wants to be, no, she also can’t be hurt while she wears that person’s skin! That’s like a Mystique 2.0 version and I’d be so ready to have superpowers like that! XD Of course I’d try not to get killed while wearing another person’s skin, because really, that would be more than just unfair to the poor person who would have to die. Still, the sheer possibility of being a different person every day or choosing your favourites to change every once in a while, just amazing! It doesn’t really surprise me that Jude became an assassin with skills like that; I can’t help but feel like there is way more to her character than we ever got to see though. I still have so many question marks when it comes to Jude and the more I read about her the more intrigued I became. I just hope that some mysteries will be solved in the third book because for now I’m left wondering and I’m getting a serious headache whenever I think too hard about it. *lol*<br /><br /><i>”Was it worth it? Syd had asked her that night, when she confessed to giving up her face, her life, herself. And it was, it was, but that didn’t stop June from craving the light of recognition in someone’s eyes. The comfort of being seen, being known.”</i><br /><br /><b>The relationships &amp; ships:</b><br /><br /><u>Victor &amp; Sydney:</u><br /><br /><i>”Sydney, I am alive because of you,” he said firmly. Tears spilled down Syd’s cheeks. Victor reached out and touched her shoulder. “You saved me.”<br />She met his eyes then, ice blue laced with red. “But I broke you.”</i> <br /><br />Aww those two! I loved to see Victor’s gentle side and no matter how much he tried to deny that he loved Sydney, he actually did/does! Syd felt terrible for causing him so much pain, but funnily enough Victor never held it against her. He always knew that her powers are limited and he tried to protect her from the truth. Well, at least as long as he could. It had to come out eventually and my heart broke for both of them when it did. &gt;_&lt; To leave her with Mitch and Dol was the right decision even though it hurt to see them part. But Sydney knew because she’s probably the only person, aside from Mitch, who knows when Vic is lying. T_T I just hope that Victor finds a solution and that they will reunite at some point. Their story isn’t over yet and I’m convinced they’ll meet each other again. &lt;3<br /><br /><i>”He could read the question in her face. It was the same one crashing through his own head.<br />What have I done?”</i><br /><br /><i>”There’s something I have to do.” Sydney was already shaking her head, but Victor reached out and put a hand on her cheek, the gesture so strange, so gentle, it stopped her cold.<br />“Syd,” he said, “look at me.”</i><br /><br /><u>Victor &amp; Eli:</u><br /><br /><i>”It frightened and thrilled Eli, to be seen, and to see himself reflected. Not all of himself – they were still so different – but there was something vital, a core of the same precious metal glinting through the rock.”</i><br /><br />How come those two men barely had any page time together, but their chemistry was still off the charts?! It’s so damn obvious that in some twisted sort of way they are in love with each other. Their obsession and the fact they can’t let go is indication enough. I mean Eli thinks Victor is dead but still talks to his ghost?! You usually only do that with loved ones! And I swear, I could feel Eli’s relief when he found out that Victor isn’t dead. He wants to kill him once again? That’s just an excuse to see him! They both need each other, they give each other purpose and I wonder what’s going to happen with Victor now that Eli is truly dead. Or is he? I’m still not all too convinced that he’s really gone! I mean what if Dr. Haverty’s drug didn’t take?! Or its effect weakened? Is it possible for Eli to heal even if he’s dead? Would he be able to come back? ADFKASDKFADAKLMNÖ! Talk about things that boggle the mind. I guess I’ll only get answers once I read book 3! &gt;_&lt; (whenever it will come out. Ahhhhh! T_T) <br /><br /><i>”Victor wondered if that was why EON hadn’t gotten closer. Not because their pet had failed to see Victor’s hand in the killings, but because he had.”</i> <br /><br /><i>”Victor stared at the wall as if it were still a window. “He doesn’t know how patient you are,” he said. “Doesn’t know you like I do.”<br />Eli cleaned the blood from his hands.<br />“No,” he said softly. “No one ever has.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Run, thought Victor, and he could see the response in Eli’s coiled frame. <br />Chase me.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Victor.” A pause. “You were supposed to stay dead.”<br />“It didn’t take.”</i><br /><br /><u>Sydney &amp; June:</u><br /><br /><i>”June could think of a dozen reasons to make sure Victor was dead, and only one to stay her hand. <br />Sydney.”</i><br /><br />So what exactly has been going on between those two? I have a lot of theories about June’s motives but I don’t know if any of them hits close to home. My first theory is that she’s in love with Sydney and a lot of the things she thought seemed to confirm that suspicion. I mean she referred to Syd as “her girl” and she didn’t only want to protect her but also wanted her to choose her over Victor. A person she knows Syd loves. Mhmm... but then again with the little we know about her past she could also be related to Syd? I don’t know how exactly but it could be possible? ARGH! I have no idea, seriously for all I know June could be her grandma and I’m not even kidding here. *lol* June is the most opaque character I ever encountered because we got NOTHING about her background. Well, at least nothing tangible. I get the feeling Schwab made her like that on purpose and I’m sure we’ll see a lot of her in book three. Considering Syd deleted her number from her phone it might take some while until they meet again though. &gt;_&lt;<br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br />This sequel was everything I hoped for and even more! &lt;3 I loved to read about all the new players that came into the game, I was happy to read about the old ones and I still can’t get enough of their morally ambiguous stance on certain things. The world needs more books like this and I’m so ready to read them all! And yes, I’m going to admit it: I’m Victor Vale trash and I’ll never be sorry for it! *lol* Can we have book three now, Victoria? XD</span>
  <a data-text-id="11595145684621633325" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1407336584" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1407336584" />
    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1407336584?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781785652486" href="/book/show/40139338-vengeful">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=i-fell-in-love">i-fell-in-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1407336584" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14165238248545176571">I'm currently debating between a 4 or 5 stars, but needless to say that I had the best time reading this book.<br/><br/>I didn't get bored once. It was thrilling, the character analysis was stunning and the pacing was beautifully set. <br/>The world of EO's got bigger and better, more fascinating and ludicrous. More morally grey characters were introduced, Victor and Eli got more despicable and lovable with each page. Mitch, Doll and Sydney constantly turned my heart into mush. <br/>And don't even get me started on</span>
  <span id="freeText14165238248545176571" style="display:none">I'm currently debating between a 4 or 5 stars, but needless to say that I had the best time reading this book.<br><br>I didn't get bored once. It was thrilling, the character analysis was stunning and the pacing was beautifully set. <br>The world of EO's got bigger and better, more fascinating and ludicrous. More morally grey characters were introduced, Victor and Eli got more despicable and lovable with each page. Mitch, Doll and Sydney constantly turned my heart into mush. <br>And don't even get me started on Marcella. <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1572539235ra/28382034.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved her! <br>Desperately need more. I can read about these psychopaths and Sydney and Mitch forever. <br><br>------------- <br><br>Time to get lost in Merit City.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2681739804" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2681739804?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Teodora " class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Teodora " href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"> Teodora </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781785652486" href="/book/show/40139338-vengeful">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=sf">sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=on-app">on-app</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=adult-new-adult">adult-new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2681739804" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer521631743231116970">5/5 ⭐<br/><br/><i>
  <b>“You’re not blessed, or divine, or burdened. You’re a science experiment.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>When I didn’t think V.E. could become more mind-blowing, newsflash, she does.<br/>With this.<br/>I mean omg.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>
    <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2681740494' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vicious</a>
  </b>
</i>? Fucking loved it. <i>
  <b>Vengeful</b>
</i>? Fucking masterpiece.<br/><br/>The story somehow manages to become even darker, the action even more precipitated, too much detail but still enough to make the story real. The plot is even more complicated because there are many new characters entering scene, each and every on</span>
  <span id="freeText521631743231116970" style="display:none">5/5 ⭐<br><br><i>
  <b>“You’re not blessed, or divine, or burdened. You’re a science experiment.”</b>
</i><br><br>When I didn’t think V.E. could become more mind-blowing, newsflash, she does.<br>With this.<br>I mean omg.<br><br><i>
  <b>
    <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2681740494" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a>
  </b>
</i>? Fucking loved it. <i>
  <b>Vengeful</b>
</i>? Fucking masterpiece.<br><br>The story somehow manages to become even darker, the action even more precipitated, too much detail but still enough to make the story real. The plot is even more complicated because there are many new characters entering scene, each and every one of them with their own personality and intense power so, again, V.E.’s mind scares the chickenshit out of me sometimes, but most of the time I think that’s just pure evil genius.<br><br>Because there are other characters making up the action, there is also a certain change of pace when it comes to the fluidity of the story itself.<br><br>Still, there are huge time lapses, from five years in the past, to three weeks in the past, to fourteen years in the past and so on. To that, add the life story of a few new characters and there you go, a nice vegetable soup for all of us to enjoy.<br><br>This is a book ruled by the thirst for power and revenge and by some sort of desperate search for something that might look like hope, but too twisted to be it.<br><br>Each of the important characters of the book has a certain level of need – one might need hope, another might need recognition, another might need love, another reassurance. It is very interesting to see how each and every desire affects the personality of the characters and turns them to the darker side of their mind.<br><br><i>
  <b>“I don’t want to survive. I want to thrive.”</b>
</i><br><br>I loved the fact that all of the characters (new and old) have their own things going on but somehow, everything they do ends up interconnected so it just becomes a big, messy mess. It honestly amazes me how ruthless and brutal are the lives of the characters. Their background and upbringing, their own experiences make up the whole road full of decisions they made for themselves in order to become the actors who stay now in front of us and act.<br><br>One thing I noticed is that the whole vibe of this installment, besides the dark mood going on, is definitely the evil sexy one. This book is evil sexy and I mean it – from the mere presence of Victor Vale to Marcella and Marcus’s hot relationship.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600949617ra/30147415.gif" width="361" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Marcella Riggins</b> née Morgan is the character I felt attracted to the most – she is gorgeous, smart, powerful, ruthless and fearless and she’s damn sassy and dramatic. She proves that no matter what your genre is, the power calls to those who want it true. No man can stand straight in from of Marcella, because she knows how to bring them down.<br><br>I bloody loved her, even though she was supposed to be the bad guy of the book. Some of my favourite scenes of the book are actually hers because – she is a bloody queen of dramatics <i>and I was living for her shows.</i><br><br><i>
  <b>“Men look at anyone with power and see only a threat, an obstacle in their path. They never have the sense to see power for what it really is.” <br>“And what is that?” asked June. <br>“Potential.”</b>
  <i><br><br>I also liked <b>June</b> and I strongly believe that we are going to see more of her in the next <i><b>Villains</b></i> book, because she felt too important to be left behind and also we don’t know much about her, even though there is definitely a lot behind her thousand masks.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515546331ra/24864021.gif" width="394" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I wanted more <b>Victor</b>. That is for sure. My favourite oh-not-so-evil-though villain needed more action. I wanted to see his struggle and to witness his mind at work. Because to me, Victor Vale could sit and watch paint dry in a dark room and I’d be fascinated by the sight. No kidding.<br><br>Something that I didn’t think possible though is that somehow I started liking Eli in this book. There was this other dimension of him that I craved to find out and now that I have, he actually makes a lot of sense. And I wanted more of him and Victor to happen. I loved their crazy dynamics in the first book and I didn’t want that to end so fast. (Confession: I think I actually ship them together). <br><br>I’m super impressed with this sequel from the <i><b>Villains</b></i> series. It was darker, more complex and deeper than the first book, the whole atmosphere shifting slightly in Schwab’s characteristic way. I truly can say that I fell in love with evil souls and I’m not ashamed to admit that right here and right now. My own evil soul is happy with that so I’m at piece.<br><br><i><b>“The life I had is gone. There’s no getting it back. I’d rather make a new one. A better one. One where I don’t have to pretend to be weak to survive.”</b></i></i>
</i></span>

<div id="review_2309801575" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2309801575" />
    <a title="Faith M ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29390149-faith-m"><img alt="Faith M ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587515873p2/29390149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2309801575?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faith M ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faith M ✨" href="/user/show/29390149-faith-m">Faith M ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765387523" href="/book/show/37534835-vengeful">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=cover-porn">cover-porn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=mc-boi">mc-boi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=get-thee-behind-me-satan">get-thee-behind-me-satan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=dont-believe-the-hype">dont-believe-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=why-did-i-read-this-exactly">why-did-i-read-this-exactly</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=feminist-but-not-actually">feminist-but-not-actually</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2309801575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11443762821086905736">Good grief I'm finally done with this.<br/><br/>I'm disappointed. I'm underwhelmed. I'm frankly a little pissed off. I went into this book with the excitement of a giddy child and came out a crone hardened by sheer boredom and anger (the worst kind). I was happy with the story, so very happy, but once Marcella (a new addition AKA the lady on the cover) mutinied and became the star of the show, around the 50% mark, I found myself dreading reading this.<br/><br/>I don't want this to be a long review so I'm going to b</span>
  <span id="freeText11443762821086905736" style="display:none">Good grief I'm finally done with this.<br /><br />I'm disappointed. I'm underwhelmed. I'm frankly a little pissed off. I went into this book with the excitement of a giddy child and came out a crone hardened by sheer boredom and anger (the worst kind). I was happy with the story, so very happy, but once Marcella (a new addition AKA the lady on the cover) mutinied and became the star of the show, around the 50% mark, I found myself dreading reading this.<br /><br />I don't want this to be a long review so I'm going to be more brief than I usually am, especially when I have so many feelings. Here are my general feelings about the characters, the plot, and the themes of the book:<br /><br />I found that all the veteran characters were cardboard cutouts of their former selves. They weren't really there long enough, their feelings and thoughts weren't touched on enough, to really warrant any feelings on my part. Victor was reduced to a hand flicking, wall leaning, tired guy who did things Victor would never do; Sydney was just meh and Mitch didn't drink nearly enough chocolate milk, though I did appreciate the extra time spent on Eli (though in the present, he wasn't nearly as entrancing as he had been in the past and in Vicious). Stell was back, and I actually really liked him. He was the only person who acted like a person, and I really appreciated that.<br /><br />The new additions were mostly wallpaper. June had no logical motives. Both her and Marcella got their revenges way too soon and too easily to really hold any tension. While the new powers were interesting, I was constantly confused about the state of clothing in regards to June's ability. Basically, she can shapeshift into anyone living that she touches (minusing EOs) and glimpse into their most basic fundamental character aspects. And she also takes...their outfit? What about clothing she puts on separately? Can she remove the clothing? If she wants a specific outfit, does she have to go looking for someone wearing it?<br /><br />Jonathan, another new addition, started out as a real person and literally became a cardboard cutout (okay not literally but pretty darn close). He just stood there. He rarely spoke. He always wore sunglasses even though everyone knew where he was looking. I forgot that he even existed for a moment.<br /><br />Dr Haverty was okay, but a little cliche and convenient, and I wish he'd stayed around longer instead of popping up right when I'd completely forgotten he was a character.<br /><br />Marcella...😒 Marcella was just Aelin Galathynius if you took away the tragic backstory. She's evil for the sake of it, black and white with no trace of grey, and a straight up psychopath. She tries to use feminism to support her ridiculous and unethical behavior and somehow...people agree? Like <i>real</i> people? She makes little snide comments about how men are always underestimating women who are ambitious, how they always call them crazy. No, lady, you are actually crazy. It's not just men saying that. Sydney isn't crazy. Sydney has morals. No one calls Sydney crazy (except for maybe Eli, but he's even more crazy). She said and did a lot of things that undermine real misogyny. She wasn't been underestimated or abused when male characters got mad at her for not holding up her end of the deal. She was being treated reasonably under the circumstances. Yes, her power of ruination was cool, but she used it as proof she is to be worshipped when she doesn't deserved to even be liked. I didn't know if this was intentional or not because the book didn't give me any clear message.<br /><br />And that brings me to the general theme of this book. Or rather, the lack of a theme. It had no direction, had no point to make. There was no greyness to anything. There were the people we're supposed to see as good guys and those who were obviously villains. There was no unique and interesting philosophy, no real conflict. It was character-driven but didn't have any character tension. Scenes that were obviously supposed to be hardhitting and important character moments lacked any kind of tension whatsoever. They felt stale and boring. The first half of this book was promising, but it didn't keep that promise.<br /><br /><blockquote>Every end may be a new beginning, but every beginning had to end.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="11443762821086905736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
